10 afios del natalicio

En este 28 de encro de 1963. se cumplen
del apéstol de nussra patria Jesé Marti

Marti fue orador. poeta. prosista, critica, novel.sta, periodists.
maestro, diplomatic, revolucionana, estadista, héroe y mértir,

Fue el cubano que organizé sus compatriotas d'spersos para
Mevarlos a la guerra del 95. esmpa vinma de la gran lucha nacional
por la Independencia politica de Espai.t. A ceta aspiracién funda-
mental de su vida consderd sniesolublemente undo ! irrevocable
achelo de la redescion econémica.

Su ideario econSmico y social: asi como su visiéa de la proble-
mince americana y su concepto de Li cultura y de ty educacién, han
cobrado vigeacia con la Revolson, Caburas. Ie cay ba hecho rea:
nocd su sucto de una Republica Cerdattersmente bre,

tamente en la Jurentud Socislista,
Mas tarde se hizo gastronémico
sin abandonar sus actividades
rerolucionarias— y finalmente, tras el triunfo de ta Re
volucién, cursé una escuela de instruccién y pasd a des
‘empeiaar Iq tara de orientador revolucionario.

Andrés Cazalla Perera, de 26 aiios, era lo que se
Hama un.abrero ejemplar, Natural de Sabanilla —de
la misma tierra en que cayé— también de pequeiio
trabajé como obrero agricola. Ya hombre, comenzi en
la ciudad a trabajar coro chofer en una tintoreria. Las
inclemencias de la vida dificil, de} trabajo asalariado,
fueron formando su espiritu. Mds tarde la Revolucion
¥ las experiencias de todo nuestro pueblo conjormarian
inalmente si conciencia. Miliciano entre los primeros
asd a integrar un batollén y con éste particips en las
acciones det Escambray y en las reservas que fueron a
Playa Girén. En el trabajo que iltimamente desempe-
fiaba sentia de cerca la obra de la Revolucién. dialogaba
con los trabajadores, participaba en Ia labor de Mevarles
las ideas revolucionarias. Con sus compaicros tuo
siempre una actitud ejemplar. :

La franqueza, ct entusiasmo y la jovialidad permanen-
te de Giraido Mora “Nikita” para sus companeros—
¥ la seriedad. el compaiierismo y la encille= de Andrés
Cazalla, estarén siempre unidas on ef recuerdo de tos
que les conocivron, a la idea de dos companvros que
supieron ser ejemplo de revolucionarios por el tesin,
la lirmeza y ta fe en el triunfo definitive de nuestro
pueblo que demostraron siempre en su trabajo con
nosotros.

El crimen no quedaré impune. La Revolucién casti-
gard a sus asesinos. ¥ el ejemplo de los que caveron,
come el de todos nuestros hermanos caidos, fortaleceré
ain més nuestra decision inquebrantable de dar hasta
nucstro tiltimo alivnto ¥ nuestra tiltima gota de sangre
por la causa de la independencia y def socialismo.

28 February 1963

MEMORANDUM FOR THE RECORD
SUBJECT: LITAMIL-9, Report of TDY, Andrew S. Parmers

va

1. During 21-26 February 1963, Andrew S. PARMERS
travelled from Headquarters to Mexico City on TDY to train
LITAMIL-9 on various clandestine, operational, techniques,
including SW. ‘Upon arrival in Mexico City PARMERS ascertained
that LITAMIL-9 allegedly becdsS of moral inhibitions, was
unwilling to receive training and also unwilling to accept the
SW syst@és Headquarters had issued for him, and which PARMERS
had carried to Mexico City. Nevertheless, PARMERS met LITAMIL-9
three times to determine the agents precise objections and to
overcome them if possible. Although the agents general
resistance was not overcome, PARMERS did review with LITAMIL-9
clandestine methods and techniques in a general way.

2. The first meeting was held at the Station case
officers home, with the Case Officer present. LITAMIL-9 ex-
plained his reasons for refusing to be trained and for not
being willing to communicate in SW with KUBARK while in Cuba.
Generally LITAMIL-9 claimed that he is very nervous, and
incapable of performing clandestine tasks without having a
nervous breakdown and at the same time getting himself caught
in the act because of his general incompetancy. Also, LITAMIL-9
was planning to stay at his brothers home in Cuba, ‘and felt
it would be unethical and immoral for him to be communicating
clandestinely with KUBARK while accepting the hospitality of
his brother and siste: ay who are staunch supporters of the
Castro regime. These obviously had already been
presented to the Case Officer who had already concluded that
LITAMIL-9 could not be moved from his position. The agent
furthermore, felt that there was no need for training or SW
since he would be returning to Mexico after only three months
in Cuba. He displayed a cable he had just received from his
father answering LITAMIL-9's query as to what might be his
next assignment. The cable stated that LITAMIL-9 would most
likely return to his present post in Mexico. The agent there-
fore felt that upon his return to Mexico City, he could be
debriefed by his Case Officer. LITAMIL-S rejected all attempts
to convince him of our need for currezt info from inside Cuba.
He was adament when we pointed out that he might not return to
Mexico City as hoped, but might bave to remain in Cuba, having
‘no means of contact. If this happens he plans to resign his
position and return to Mexico as a private citizen, since he
already is a registered "resident" of Mexico.

ferry


3. On Friday, 24 February, PARMERS spent most of
day visiting alone with LITAMIL-9 at the latter's apart-
tt; By the end of. the day LITAMIL-9 had softened a little
Jand had revealed: Some ‘of the personality traits mentioned
below. LITAMIL-9 also agreed to communicate with his Case
Officer through open code in letters to his brother in Mexico
City. He also was willing to meet inside KUBARK, preferably
if the contact was'a diplomat but not Cuban. He agreed to
teke-a set of cuff links as bona fides. As a suggestion, he
mentioned that his friend, The Swiss Ambassador, now serving
in Madrid, Spain, would be an ideal contact. In revealing how
such a contact could be performed and in discussing LITAMIL-9
modus vevendi in Cubs, there was considerable discussione
concerning operational Security aud clandestine procedures me
LITAMIL-9 can apply while in Cuba. :

4. LITAMIL-9 during this meeting also presented,

in logical sequence, his reasons for believing that he will
return to Mexico City. Basically, he feels that between the
fact that he has many contacts in Mexico City (where he has
lived and worked for many years) and the fact that his sister-
in-law in Cuba has a responsible position with considerable
influence in the Castro Government, he, LITAMIL-9, will be re-
assigned to his present post in Mexico City after three months
of leave, consultations, and training in Cuba.

5. :The third meeting ocurred in the evening of
25 February, in a car pick up situation, with the Case Officer
present, This time, LITAMIL-9 was less willing to communicate
with KUBARK while in Cuba than he had been during the previous
meeting, but with some reluctance, agreed to the use of open
code and to be contacted by some diplomat. This meeting, there-
fore, was a routine operational meeting, with his Case Officer
in charge.

6. Based upon their three meetings, PARMERS formed
the following opinions of LITAMIL-9: He is a shrewd oppor-
tunist, willing to colloborate with KUBARK against the Castro
Government, but not. to the point where his personal security
is endangered. He dislikes the Castro Regime because it has
fumbled so badly, and because the current Cuban officials are
crude and incompetant. He greatly admires the American people,
but definitely feels that we are merely concerned about our
own national security and well-being. LITAMIL-9 owes his
first loyalty to the fine arts, kas lattle Patriotic feelings
towards Cuba, since he has lived in Mexico for so many years,
and has declared himself to be a resident of Mexico. He is
now serving the Cuban Government simply because he had an
opportunity (through his sister-in-law) to achieve official
status and .ncome and still remain in Mexico where most of his



Sct nd

Sasa! Sa cpenabss cial 8 Ciel tat sn

personal friends reside.

7. Although at first appearance, and according to
- his“own opiméon statements, LITAMIL-9 appears to be extremely
nervous because of his’clandestine activities in behalf of
KUBARK and ‘against Cuba, after ‘some discussion it was apparent
‘that he actually relishes these clandestine actions that he
“would have. engaged in then long before he did, and that he
would ‘have continued a covert relationship with KUBARK even after
Castro falls, serving either. in Mexico (where he has many
contacts of interest to KUBARK) or in Cuba in some post in
some future government. He has excellent rapport with his
present KUBARK case officer. He states that as long as KUBARK
remains willing to accept that he has definite personal limi-
tations, (since he can perform only those clandestixo tasks
related to his cover and cannot be trained or induced to do
anything else) he will gladly continue collaborating with
KUBARK as long as desired.

8. Actually, PARMERS feels that LITAMIL-9 would
do most anything we would desire if KU"ARK would someday
establish some control over him. His present remarks concerning
his moral qualms are artificial. He has great appreciation
for shrewdness and double play, and openly admits having
engaged in it all h:s life. On many occasions he admits that
he has accomoiated himself to a situation for profit or because
he knew that he could turn the tables eventually on his ad-
versaries. When he is off-guard he admits to being a cool
operater who can scheme and work behind his adversaries’ backs.
He shows many signs of enjoying doing what he does for and
with his present KUBARK case officer.

9. In summary, Although LI LITAMIL-9 did not sceent fe
a e

raining or S staida7d sense, PAR’
azents reluctai ba in his desire

[L<_agetif—is competent, 3 mofal inhibitions are
faked. He is cunvinced that he will return to Mexico soon, and
desires to continue serving KUBARK if no greater risk is in-
volved. Since KUBARK at present has no clear control (monetary
or ideological) over LITAMIL-9, it was difficult to impose
XUBARK's will over him. But he is very willing to perform for
KUBARK within tae limitations he :-ts, and if somedy we can
satisfy some personal need he might have, he has the pot ential
of becoming a good controlled agent for KUBARK. He is intell-
igent and by nature he seems to iastinctively conduct his
clandestine operations in a secure manner.

Andrew S. Parmers
OTR Training Officer

ON 49 FEB 63, GERARDO SANCHEZ ROBERT, CUBAN CONSUL JATAICA,
DELIVERED LTR FLON “CONCHITA* FERNANDEZ DATED 2 FEB 63 TO LITAMIL-9.
DLTR MARKED “PERSONAL”, “ALA MANC. LTR ASKED L+9 RETURN HAVA WHERE
COULD DISCUSS CASE RE RETURN MEXI. STATED NOT RIGHT REKAIN TWO OR
THREE MORE MONTHS NEXY THIS TINE. SAID PROPER “RESIGN WHILE MAVA
NOT OVERSEAS. . IN SHORT, LTR OSTENSIBLY ASKED L-9 RETURN HAVA. NEVER
THELESS, LTR ALSO TOLD Le9 "MAKE THIS OWN DECISION". L+9, DIS
APPOINTED, PLANS CALL RANGN SINOBAS ASIDE AND GIVE HIN GOOD INDICATION
THAT IF HE ASKED RETURN HAVA HE'LL RESIGN, L-9 OPINION SINOBAS WHO
UNDER. GREAT DEAL PRESSURE PER REF 8 WILL ADVISS FOREIGN OFFICE
PREFERASLE KEEP L+9 MEXI AS VILL RESIGN IF RECALLED, L-9 YELIVES
SINOBAS VILL DO UTMOST AVOID L+9 *LOSS* PRESENT CIRCURSTANCES,
IN ADDITION, TERESA PROENZA STILL HAVA AND NOT EXPECTED RETURN Two
MORE WEEKS, “SHE OTHER CULTURAL ATTACHE AND "LOSS* Le9° THIS TINE WouLD

BE SERIOUS BLOW SINOBAS AND CUSAN ENSASSY. ‘STATICN AND L-9 BELIEVE
